```json output_result
Pro 36 hours 36 hours
Max 24 hours 18 hours
Notes:
First Reply Time: Maximum time from ticket creation to the  rst customer contact.
Second Reply Time: If the  rst reply exceeds the deadline, you must send an apology email
stating that the next reply will be sent within this time frame.
6.2 Templates
Note: The Placeholder in this section should be replaced to real values.

promised timeframe.

7. Additional Operational Metrics (Non-SLA)
These performance metrics are tracked for internal monitoring purposes only and have no bearing on
customer SLAs.
7.1 Conformance Rate
Calculated monthly as the percentage of internal performance targets achieved.
Segmented by:
Infrastructure uptime
Average incident resolution by internal priority
Patch cycle completion rate
7.2 Service Credit Eligibility (Internal Reference to AWS Model)
Service Credits (if issued) are applied as a percentage discount on future internal cross-
department billing.
Maximum internal service credit per month: 30% of the allocated operational budget for the
affected service.
Credits are not transferable outside the organization.
8. Internal Reporting Work ow
 . Detection: Automated systems log uptime and incident metrics every  ve minutes.
 . Classi cation: Technical operations team assigns internal priority levels (P1, P2, P3).
 . Action: Appropriate recovery, patching, or monitoring adjustments.
 . Documentation: Metrics stored for quarterly performance review.
9. SLA Exclusions

=== Page 5 ===
Page 5 of 5The following do not count towards SLA performance metrics:
Authorized maintenance during the scheduled monthly window.
Downtime due to third-party upstream providers beyond MCP‚Äôs control.
Customer-requested delays or refusal of recommended action.
Failures in unsupported third-party software.
10. Glossary
First Reply Time: Interval between ticket creation and  rst customer contact.
Second Reply Time: Interval to follow-up after overdue  rst reply.
Maintenance Window: Designated time for pre-scheduled service work.
Incident Recovery: Process to restore unavailable systems or services.
Conformance Rate: Measure of how often internal targets are met.
```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "\nSELECT \n    t.ID,
	\n    t.TICKET_NUMBER,
	\n    t.SUBJECT,
	\n    t.DESCRIPTION,
	\n    t.PRIORITY,
	\n    t.TICKET_TYPE,
	\n    t.STATUS,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT,
	\n    t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT,
	\n    t.USER_ID,
	\n    u.NAME as USER_NAME,
	\n    u.EMAIL as USER_EMAIL,
	\n    u.SERVICE_LEVEL,
	\n    u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Basic' THEN 72\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Pro' THEN 36\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Max' THEN 24\n    END as FIRST_REPLY_TIME_HOURS,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Basic' THEN 72\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Pro' THEN 36\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Max' THEN 18\n    END as SECOND_REPLY_TIME_HOURS,
	\n    TIMESTAMPDIFF(HOUR,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) as HOURS_SINCE_CREATION\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\nORDER BY u.SERVICE_LEVEL DESC,
	t.CREATED_AT ASC\n"
}

```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "\nSELECT \n    t.ID,
	\n    t.TICKET_NUMBER,
	\n    t.SUBJECT,
	\n    t.DESCRIPTION,
	\n    t.PRIORITY,
	\n    t.TICKET_TYPE,
	\n    t.STATUS,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT,
	\n    t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT,
	\n    t.USER_ID,
	\n    u.NAME as USER_NAME,
	\n    u.EMAIL as USER_EMAIL,
	\n    u.SERVICE_LEVEL,
	\n    u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' THEN 72\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' THEN 36\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' THEN 24\n    END as FIRST_REPLY_TIME_HOURS,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' THEN 72\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' THEN 36\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' THEN 18\n    END as SECOND_REPLY_TIME_HOURS,
	\n    TIMESTAMPDIFF(HOUR,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) as HOURS_SINCE_CREATION\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\n  AND TIMESTAMPDIFF(HOUR,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > \n      CASE \n          WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' THEN 72\n          WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' THEN 36\n          WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' THEN 24\n      END\nORDER BY \n    CASE \n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' THEN 1\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' THEN 2\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' THEN 3\n    END,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT ASC\n"
}
```

```json output_result
7. Additional Operational Metrics (Non-SLA)
These performance metrics are tracked for internal monitoring purposes only and have no bearing on
customer SLAs.
7.1 Conformance Rate
Calculated monthly as the percentage of internal performance targets achieved.
Segmented by:
Infrastructure uptime
Average incident resolution by internal priority
Patch cycle completion rate
7.2 Service Credit Eligibility (Internal Reference to AWS Model)
Service Credits (if issued) are applied as a percentage discount on future internal cross-
department billing.
Maximum internal service credit per month: 30% of the allocated operational budget for the
affected service.
Credits are not transferable outside the organization.
8. Internal Reporting Work ow
 . Detection: Automated systems log uptime and incident metrics every  ve minutes.
 . Classi cation: Technical operations team assigns internal priority levels (P1, P2, P3).
 . Action: Appropriate recovery, patching, or monitoring adjustments.
 . Documentation: Metrics stored for quarterly performance review.
9. SLA Exclusions

=== Page 5 ===
Page 5 of 5The following do not count towards SLA performance metrics:
Authorized maintenance during the scheduled monthly window.
Downtime due to third-party upstream providers beyond MCP‚Äôs control.
Customer-requested delays or refusal of recommended action.
Failures in unsupported third-party software.
10. Glossary
First Reply Time: Interval between ticket creation and  rst customer contact.
Second Reply Time: Interval to follow-up after overdue  rst reply.
Maintenance Window: Designated time for pre-scheduled service work.
Incident Recovery: Process to restore unavailable systems or services.
Conformance Rate: Measure of how often internal targets are met.
```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "SELECT \n    t.TICKET_NUMBER,
	\n    t.PRIORITY,
	\n    t.STATUS,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT,
	\n    t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT,
	\n    u.NAME as USER_NAME,
	\n    u.EMAIL as USER_EMAIL,
	\n    u.SERVICE_LEVEL,
	\n    u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Basic' THEN 72\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Pro' THEN 36\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Max' THEN 24\n    END as EXPECTED_RESPONSE_HOURS,
	\n    DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) as HOURS_SINCE_CREATION,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Basic' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 72 THEN 'OVERDUE'\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Pro' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 36 THEN 'OVERDUE'\n        WHEN u.SERVICE_LEVEL = 'Max' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 24 THEN 'OVERDUE'\n        ELSE 'ON_TIME'\n    END as SLA_STATUS\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\nAND t.STATUS = 'open'\nORDER BY \n    CASE u.SERVICE_LEVEL \n        WHEN 'Max' THEN 1\n        WHEN 'Pro' THEN 2\n        WHEN 'Basic' THEN 3\n    END,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT"
}

```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "SELECT \n    u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER,
	\n    COUNT(*) as OVERDUE_TICKETS,
	\n    STRING_AGG(t.TICKET_NUMBER || ': ' || UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL),
	',
	') as TICKET_LIST\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\nAND t.STATUS = 'open'\nAND (\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 72) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 36) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 24)\n)\nGROUP BY u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER\nORDER BY COUNT(*) DESC"
}

```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "SELECT \n    u.CUSTOMER_MANAGER,
	\n    t.TICKET_NUMBER,
	\n    UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) as SERVICE_LEVEL\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\nAND t.STATUS = 'open'\nAND (\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 72) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 36) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 24)\n)\nORDER BY \n    CASE UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) \n        WHEN 'MAX' THEN 1\n        WHEN 'PRO' THEN 2\n        WHEN 'BASIC' THEN 3\n    END,
	\n    t.CREATED_AT"
}
```

```json arguments
{
	"query": "SELECT \n    t.TICKET_NUMBER,
	\n    u.NAME as USER_NAME,
	\n    u.EMAIL as USER_EMAIL,
	\n    UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) as SERVICE_LEVEL,
	\n    CASE \n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' THEN 72\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' THEN 36\n        WHEN UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' THEN 18\n    END as SECOND_REPLY_TIME\nFROM SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.SUPPORT_TICKETS t\nJOIN SLA_MONITOR.PUBLIC.USERS u ON t.USER_ID = u.ID\nWHERE t.FIRST_RESPONSE_AT IS NULL\nAND t.STATUS = 'open'\nAND (\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'BASIC' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 72) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'PRO' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 36) OR\n    (UPPER(u.SERVICE_LEVEL) = 'MAX' AND DATEDIFF(hour,
	t.CREATED_AT,
	CURRENT_TIMESTAMP()) > 24)\n)"
}
```
